style="display:none"><th colspan="2">\n</th></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Isles of Scilly</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="/\xc9\xaa/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">\xc9\xaa</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="/i/: &#39;y&#39; in &#39;happy&#39;">i</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a>: <i lang="kw">Syllan</i> or <i><i lang="kw" title="Cornish language text">Enesek Syllan</i></i>) is an <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a> off the southwestern tip of <a href="/wiki/Cornwall" title="Cornwall">Cornwall</a>. One of the islands, <a href="/wiki/St_Agnes,_Isles_of_Scilly" title="St Agnes, Isles of Scilly">St Agnes</a>, is the most southerly point in both <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, being over 4 miles (6.4&#160;km) further south than the most southerly point of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">British mainland</a> at <a href="/wiki/Lizard_Point,_Cornwall" title="Lizard Point, Cornwall">Lizard Point</a>.\n</p><p>The population of all the islands at the 2011 census was 2,203.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Scilly forms part of the <a href="/wiki/Ceremonial_counties_of_England" title="Ceremonial counties of England">ceremonial county</a> of <a href="/wiki/Cornwall" title="Cornwall">Cornwall</a>, and some services are combined with those of Cornwall. However, since 1890, the islands have had <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_Isles_of_Scilly" title="Council of the Isles of Scilly">a separate local authority</a>. Since the passing of the Isles of Scilly Order 1930, this authority has had the status of a <a href="/wiki/County_council" title="County council">county council</a> and today is known as the Council of the Isles of Scilly.\n</p><p>The adjective "Scillonian" is sometimes used for people or things related to the archipelago. The <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Cornwall" title="Duchy of Cornwall">Duchy of Cornwall</a> owns most of the <a href="/wiki/Freehold_(law)" title="Freehold (law)">freehold land</a> on the islands. Tourism is a major part of the local economy, along with agriculture\xe2\x80\x94particularly the production of <a href="/wiki/Cut_flowers" title="Cut flowers">cut flowers</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toclevel-2 tocsection-9"><a href="#Geology"><span class="tocnumber">3.3</span> <span class="toctext">Geology</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-10"><a href="#Fauna"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Fauna</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11"><a href="#Government"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span government</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13"><a href="#Local_government"><span class="tocnumber">5.2</span> <span class="toctext">Local government</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#Flags"><span class="tocnumber">5.3</span> <span class="toctext">Flags</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15"><a href="#Emergency_services"><span class="tocnumber">5.4</span> <span class="toctext">Emergency services</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#Education"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Education</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#Economy"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Economy</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18"><a href="#Historical_context"><span class="tocnumber">7.1</span> <span class="toctext">Historical context</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19"><a href="#Tourism"><span class="tocnumber">7.2</span> <span class="toctext">Tourism</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-20"><a href="#Ornithology"><span class="tocnumber">7.2.1</span> <span class="toctext">Ornithology</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#Employment"><span class="tocnumber">7.3</span> <span class="toctext">Employment</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#Taxation"><span class="tocnumber">7.4</span> <span class="toctext">Taxation</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23"><a href="#Transport"><span class="tocnumber">7.5</span> <span class="toctext">Transport</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-24"><a href="#Tenure"><span class="tocnumber">7.6</span> <span class="toctext">Tenure</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#Culture"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Culture</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26"><a href="#People"><span class="tocnumber">8.1</span> <span class="toctext">People</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27"><a href="#Sport"><span class="tocnumber">8.2</span> <span class="toctext">Sport</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-28"><a href="#Media"><span class="tocnumber">8.3</span> <span class="toctext">Media</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-29"><a href="#Novels"><span class="tocnumber">8.4</span> <span class="toctext">Novels</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-30"><a href="#Song"><span class="tocnumber">8.5</span> <span class="toctext">Song</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31"><a href="#Notable_people"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Notable people</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isles_of_Scilly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isles_of_Scilly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The islands may correspond to the <a href="/wiki/Cassiterides" title="Cassiterides">Cassiterides</a> (<i>Tin Isles</i>) visited by the <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">Phoenicians</a> and mentioned by the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Greeks</a>. However, the archipelago itself does not contain much tin.\n</p><p>It is likely that until relatively recent times the islands were much larger and perhaps joined together into one island named Ennor. Rising sea levels flooded the central plain around 400\xe2\x80\x93500 AD, forming the current 55 islands and islets, if an island is defined as "land surrounded by water at high tide and supporting land vegetation".<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The word <i><i lang="kw" title="Cornish language text">Ennor</i></i> is a contraction of the Old Cornish<sup id="cite_ref-Dictionary_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dictionary-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> <i><i lang="kw" title="Cornish language text">En Noer</i></i> (<i><i lang="kw" title="Cornish language text">Moer</i></i>, mutated to <i><i lang="kw" title="Cornish language text">Noer</i></i>), meaning \'the land\'<sup id="cite_ref-Dictionary_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dictionary-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> or the \'great island\'.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Evidence for the older large island includes:\n</p>\n<ul><li>A description written during Roman times designates Scilly "<i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Scillonia insula</i>" in the <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_number" title="Grammatical number">singular</a>, indicating either a single island or an island much bigger than any of the others.</li>\n<li>Remains of a prehistoric farm have been found on <a href="/wiki/Nornour" class="mw-redirect" title="Nornour">Nornour</a>, which is now a small rocky <a href="/wiki/Skerry" title="Skerry">skerry</a> far too small for farming.<sup id="cite_ref-Thorgrim_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thorgrim-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> There once was an <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age_Britain" class="mw-redirect" title="Iron Age Britain">Iron Age Britain</a> community here that extended into Roman times.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> This community was likely formed by immigrants from Brittany, probably the <a href="/wiki/Veneti_(Gaul)" title="Veneti (Gaul)">Veneti</a> who were active in the tin trade that originated in <a href="/wiki/Mining_in_Cornwall_and_Devon" title="Mining in Cornwall and Devon">mining activity in Cornwall and Devon</a>.</li>\n<li>At certain low tides the sea becomes shallow enough for people to walk between some of the islands.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> This is possibly one of the sources for stories of drowned lands, e.g. <a href="/wiki/Lyonesse" title="Lyonesse">Lyonesse</a>.</li>\n<li>Ancient field walls are visible below the high tide line off some of the islands (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Samson,_Isles_of_Scilly" title="Samson, Isles of Scilly">Samson</a>).</li>\n<li>Some of the <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish language</a> place names also appear to reflect past shorelines, and former land areas.<sup id="cite_ref-Weatherhill_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Weatherhill-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>The whole of <a href="/wiki/Southern_England" title="Southern England">southern England</a> has been steadily sinking in opposition to <a href="/wiki/Post-glacial_rebound" title="Post-glacial rebound">post-glacial rebound</a> in Scotland: this has caused the <a href="/wiki/Ria" title="Ria">rias</a> (drowned river valleys) on the southern Cornish coast, e.g. <a href="/wiki/River_Fal" title="River Fal">River Fal</a> and the <a href="/wiki/River_Tamar" title="River Tamar">Tamar Estuary</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>Offshore, midway between <a href="/wiki/Land%27s_End" title="Land&#39;s End">Land\'s End</a> and the Isles of Scilly, is the supposed location of the mythical lost land of <a href="/wiki/Lyonesse" title="Lyonesse">Lyonesse</a>, referred to in <a href="/wiki/King_Arthur" title="King Arthur">Arthurian</a> literature, of which <a href="/wiki/Tristan_and_Isolde" class="mw-redirect" title="Tristan and Isolde">Tristan</a> is said to have been a prince. This may be a <a href="/wiki/Folk_memory" title="Folk memory">folk memory</a> of inundated lands, but this legend is also common among the <a href="/wiki/Britons_(historical)" class="mw-redirect" title="Britons (historical)">Brythonic</a> peoples; the legend of <a href="/wiki/Ys" title="Ys">Ys</a> is a parallel and cognate legend in <a href="/wiki/Brittany" title="Brittany">Brittany</a> as is that of <i lang="cy" title="Welsh language text"><a href="/wiki/Cantre%27r_Gwaelod" title="Cantre&#39;r Gwaelod">Cantre\'r Gwaelod</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a>.\n</p><p>Scilly has been identified as the place of exile of two heretical 4th century bishops, Instantius and Tiberianus, who were followers of <a href="/wiki/Priscillian" title="Priscillian">Priscillian</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Norse_and_Norman_period">Norse and Norman period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isles_of_Scilly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Norse and Norman period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Peter_nicolai_arbo,_olaf_tryggvasson_king.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Peter_nicolai_arbo%2C_olaf_tryggvasson_king.jpg/220px-Peter_nicolai_arbo%2C_olaf_tryggvasson_king.jpg" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Peter_nicolai_arbo%2C_olaf_tryggvasson_king.jpg/330px-Peter_nicolai_arbo%2C_olaf_tryggvasson_king.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Peter_nicolai_arbo%2C_olaf_tryggvasson_king.jpg/440px-Peter_nicolai_arbo%2C_olaf_tryggvasson_king.jpg 2x" data-file-width="460" data-file-height="294" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Peter_nicolai_arbo,_olaf_tryggvasson_king.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Olaf_I_of_Norway" class="mw-redirect" title="Olaf I of Norway">Olaf Tryggvason</a>, who visited the islands in 986. It is said an encounter with a cleric there led him to Christianise <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EmpireNorth.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/EmpireNorth.JPG/220px-EmpireNorth.JPG" width="220" height="218" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/EmpireNorth.JPG/330px-EmpireNorth.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/EmpireNorth.JPG/440px-EmpireNorth.JPG 2x" data-file-width="674" data-file-height="668" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EmpireNorth.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>At the time of <a href="/wiki/Cnut_the_Great" title="Cnut the Great">King Cnut</a>, the Isles of Scilly fell outside <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">England\'s rule</a>, as did Cornwall and Wales.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 995, <a href="/wiki/Olaf_I_of_Norway" class="mw-redirect" title="Olaf I of Norway">Olaf Tryggvason</a> became King Olaf I of <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>. Born <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 960, Olaf had raided various European cities and fought in several wars. In 986 he (supposedly) met a Christian <a href="/wiki/Clairvoyance" title="Clairvoyance">seer</a> on the Isles of Scilly. He was probably <a href="/wiki/Priscillian" title="Priscillian">Priscillian</a> and a part of the tiny Christian community that was exiled here from Spain by <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Maximus" class="mw-redirect" title="Emperor Maximus">Emperor Maximus</a> for <a href="/wiki/Priscillianism" title="Priscillianism">Priscillianism</a> and their part in the Priscilline heresy. In <a href="/wiki/Snorri_Sturluson" title="Snorri Sturluson">Snorri Sturluson</a>\'s Royal Sagas of Norway, it is stated that this seer told him:\n</p>\n<blockquote><p>Thou wilt become a renowned king, and do celebrated deeds. Many men wilt thou bring to faith and baptism, and both to thy own and others\' good; and that thou mayst have no doubt of the truth of this answer, listen to these tokens. When thou comest to thy ships many of thy people will conspire against thee, and then a battle will follow in which many of thy men will fall, and thou wilt be wounded almost to death, and carried upon a shield to thy ship; yet after seven days thou shalt be well of thy wounds, and immediately thou shalt let thyself be baptised.</p></blockquote>\n<p>The legend continues that, as the seer foretold, Olaf was attacked by a group of <a href="/wiki/Mutiny" title="Mutiny">mutineers</a> upon returning to his ships. As soon as he had recovered from his wounds, he let himself be baptised. He then stopped raiding Christian cities, and lived in England and Ireland. In 995, he used an opportunity to return to Norway. When he arrived, the <a href="/wiki/Haakon_Jarl" class="mw-redirect" title="Haakon Jarl">Haakon Jarl</a> was facing a revolt. Olaf Tryggvason persuaded the rebels to accept him as their king, and Jarl Haakon was murdered by his own slave, while he was hiding from the rebels in a pig sty.\n</p><p>With the <a href="/wiki/Norman_Conquest" class="mw-redirect" title="Norman Conquest">Norman Conquest</a>, the Isles of Scilly came more under centralised control. About 20 years later, the <a href="/wiki/Domesday_Book" title="Domesday Book">Domesday survey</a> was conducted. The islands would have formed part of the "<a href="/wiki/Exeter" title="Exeter">Exeter</a> Domesday" circuit, which included Cornwall, <a href="/wiki/Devon" title="Devon">Devon</a>, Dorset, <a href="/wiki/Somerset" title="Somerset">Somerset</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wiltshire" title="Wiltshire">Wiltshire</a>.\n</p><p>In the mid-12th century, there was reportedly a Viking attack on the Isles of Scilly, called <b><i lang="non" title="Old Norse language text">Syllingar</i></b> by the Norse,<sup id="cite_ref-OrkSaga_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OrkSaga-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> recorded in the <i><i lang="non" title="Old Norse language text"><a href="/wiki/Orkneyinga_saga" title="Orkneyinga saga">Orkneyinga saga</a></i></i>\xe2\x80\x94 <a href="/wiki/Sweyn_Asleifsson" title="Sweyn Asleifsson">Sweyn Asleifsson</a> "went south, under Ireland, and seized a barge belonging to some monks in Syllingar and plundered it."<sup id="cite_ref-OrkSaga_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OrkSaga-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> (Chap LXXIII)\n</p>\n<blockquote><p>...the three chiefs\xe2\x80\x94Swein, \xc3\x9eorbj\xc3\xb6rn and Eirik\xe2\x80\x94went out on a plundering expedition. They went first to the Su\xc3\xb0reyar [Hebrides], and all along the west to the Syllingar, where they gained a great victory in Mar\xc3\xaduh\xc3\xb6fn on Columba\'s-mass [9 June], and took much booty. Then they returned to the Orkneys.<sup id="cite_ref-OrkSaga_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OrkSaga-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<p>"<i lang="non" title="Old Norse language text">Mar\xc3\xaduh\xc3\xb6fn</i>" literally means "Mary\'s Harbour/Haven". The name does not make it clear if it referred to a harbour on a larger island than today\'s St Mary\'s, or a whole island.\n</p><p>It is generally considered that Cornwall, and possibly the Isles of Scilly, came under the dominion of the English Crown late in the reign of <a href="/wiki/%C3%86thelstan" title="\xc3\x86thelstan">\xc3\x86thelstan</a> (<abbr title="reigned">r.</abbr> 924\xe2\x80\x93939). In early times one group of islands was in the possession of a confederacy of hermits. <a href="/wiki/Henry_I_of_England" title="Henry I of England">King Henry I</a> (r. 1100\xe2\x80\x9335) gave it to the <a href="/wiki/Tavistock_Abbey" title="Tavistock Abbey">abbey of Tavistock</a> who established a priory on <a href="/wiki/Tresco,_Isles_of_Scilly" title="Tresco, Isles of Scilly">Tresco</a>, which was abolished at the <a href="/wiki/English_Reformation" title="English Reformation">Reformation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Later_Middle_Ages_and_early_modern_period">Later Middle Ages and early modern period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isles_of_Scilly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Later Middle Ages and early modern period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kernow_Hundreds.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Kernow_Hundreds.png/220px-Kernow_Hundreds.png" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Kernow_Hundreds.png/330px-Kernow_Hundreds.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Kernow_Hundreds.png/440px-Kernow_Hundreds.png 2x" data-file-width="821" data-file-height="532" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kernow_Hundreds.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Scilly was one of the <a href="/wiki/Hundreds_of_Cornwall" title="Hundreds of Cornwall">Hundreds of Cornwall</a> (formerly known as Cornish Shires) in the early 19th century.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Scilly-bartholomew02_large.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Scilly-bartholomew02_large.jpg/220px-Scilly-bartholomew02_large.jpg" width="220" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Scilly-bartholomew02_large.jpg/330px-Scilly-bartholomew02_large.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Scilly-bartholomew02_large.jpg/440px-Scilly-bartholomew02_large.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2017" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Scilly-bartholomew02_large.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Scilly Isles: map by John Bartholomew (1874)</div></div></div>\n<p>At the turn of the 14th century, the Abbot and convent of Tavistock Abbey petitioned the king,\n</p>\n<blockquote><p>stat[ing] that they hold certain isles in the sea between Cornwall and Ireland, of which the largest is called Scilly, to which ships come passing between France, Normandy, Spain, <a href="/wiki/Bayonne" title="Bayonne">Bayonne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gascony" title="Gascony">Gascony</a>, Scotland, Ireland, Wales and Cornwall: and, because they feel that in the event of a war breaking out between the kings of England and France, or between any of the other places mentioned, they would not have enough power to do justice to these sailors, they ask that they might exchange these islands for lands in Devon, saving the churches on the islands appropriated to them.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<p>William le Poer, coroner of Scilly, is recorded in 1305 as being worried about the <a href="/wiki/List_of_shipwrecks_of_the_Isles_of_Scilly" title="List of shipwrecks of the Isles of Scilly">extent of wrecking in the islands</a>, and sending a petition to the King. The names provide a wide variety of origins, e.g. Robert and Henry Sage (English), Richard de Tregenestre (Cornish), Ace de Veldre (French), Davy Gogch (possibly Welsh, or Cornish), and Adam le Fuiz Yaldicz (Spanish?).\n</p><p>It is not known at what point the islanders stopped speaking the <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish language</a>, but the language seems to have gone into decline in Cornwall beginning in the <a href="/wiki/Late_Middle_Ages" title="Late Middle Ages">Late Middle Ages</a>; it was still dominant between the islands and Bodmin at the time of the Reformation, but it suffered an accelerated decline thereafter. The islands appear to have lost the old Celtic language before parts of <a href="/wiki/Penwith" title="Penwith">Penwith</a> on the mainland, in contrast to the history of <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a> or <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Scottish Gaelic">Scottish Gaelic</a>.\n</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/English_Civil_War" title="English Civil War">English Civil War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Roundhead" title="Roundhead">Parliamentarians</a> captured the isles, only to see their garrison mutiny and return the isles to the <a href="/wiki/Cavalier" title="Cavalier">Royalists</a>. By 1651 the Royalist governor, <a href="/wiki/John_Granville,_1st_Earl_of_Bath" title="John Granville, 1st Earl of Bath">Sir John Grenville</a>, was using the islands as a base for <a href="/wiki/Privateering" class="mw-redirect" title="Privateering">privateering</a> raids on Commonwealth and Dutch shipping. The Dutch admiral <a href="/wiki/Maarten_Tromp" title="Maarten Tromp">Maarten Tromp</a> sailed to the isles and on arriving on 30 May 1651 demanded compensation. In the  absence of compensation or a satisfactory reply, he declared war on England in June. It was during this period that the <a href="/wiki/Three_Hundred_and_Thirty_Five_Years%27_War" title="Three Hundred and Thirty Five Years&#39; War">Three Hundred and Thirty Five Years\' War</a> started between the isles and the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>.\n</p><p>In June 1651, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Blake_(admiral)" title="Robert Blake (admiral)">Admiral Robert Blake</a> recaptured the isles for the <a href="/wiki/Roundhead" title="Roundhead">Parliamentarians</a>. Blake\'s initial attack on <a href="/wiki/Old_Grimsby" title="Old Grimsby">Old Grimsby</a> failed, but the next attacks succeeded in taking <a href="/wiki/Tresco,_Isles_of_Scilly" title="Tresco, Isles of Scilly">Tresco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bryher,_Isles_of_Scilly" class="mw-redirect" title="Bryher, Isles of Scilly">Bryher</a>. Blake placed a battery on Tresco to fire on <a href="/wiki/St._Mary%27s,_Isles_of_Scilly" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Mary&#39;s, Isles of Scilly">St Mary\'s</a>, but one of the guns exploded, killing its crew and injuring Blake. A second battery proved more successful. Subsequently, Grenville and Blake negotiated terms that permitted the Royalists to surrender honourably. The Parliamentary forces then set to fortifying the islands. They built <a href="/wiki/Cromwell%27s_Castle" title="Cromwell&#39;s Castle">Cromwell\'s Castle</a>\xe2\x80\x94a gun platform on the west side of Tresco\xe2\x80\x94using materials scavenged from an earlier gun platform further up the hill. Although this poorly sited earlier platform dated back to the 1550s, it is now referred to as <a href="/wiki/King_Charles%27s_Castle" title="King Charles&#39;s Castle">King Charles\'s Castle</a>.\n</p><p>During the night of 22 October 1707, the isles were the scene of <a href="/wiki/Scilly_naval_disaster_of_1707" title="Scilly naval disaster of 1707">one of the worst maritime disasters</a> in British history, when out of a fleet of 21 Royal Navy ships headed from <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a> to <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth" title="Portsmouth">Portsmouth</a>, six were driven onto the cliffs. Four of the ships sank or capsized, with at least 1,450 dead, including the commanding <a href="/wiki/Admiral" title="Admiral">admiral</a> Sir <a href="/wiki/Cloudesley_Shovell" title="Cloudesley Shovell">Cloudesley Shovell</a>.\n</p><p>There is evidence for inundation by the tsunami caused by the <a href="/wiki/1755_Lisbon_earthquake" title="1755 Lisbon earthquake">1755 Lisbon earthquake</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Banerjee_et_al._2001._15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Banerjee_et_al._2001.-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The islands appear to have been raided frequently by <a href="/wiki/Barbary_pirate" class="mw-redirect" title="Barbary pirate">Barbary pirates</a> to enslave residents to support the <a href="/wiki/Barbary_slave_trade" title="Barbary slave trade">Barbary slave trade</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governors_of_Scilly">Governors of Scilly</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isles_of_Scilly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Governors of Scilly">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Governors_of_Scilly" title="List of Governors of Scilly">List of Governors of Scilly</a></div>\n<p>An early governor of Scilly was <a href="/w/index.php?title=Thomas_Godolphin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Thomas Godolphin (page does not exist)">Thomas Godolphin</a>, whose son <a href="/wiki/Francis_Godolphin_(1540%E2%80%931608)" title="Francis Godolphin (1540\xe2\x80\x931608)">Francis</a> received a lease on the Isles in 1568. They were styled <i>Governors of Scilly</i> and the Godolphins and their Osborne relatives held this position until 1834. In 1834 <a href="/wiki/Augustus_Smith_(politician)" title="Augustus Smith (politician)">Augustus John Smith</a> acquired the lease from the Duchy for \xc2\xa320,000.<sup id="cite_ref-inflation-UK_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inflation-UK-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Smith created the title <i>Lord Proprietor of the Isles of Scilly</i> for himself, and many of his actions were unpopular. The lease remained in his family until it expired for most of the Isles in 1920 when ownership reverted to the Duchy of Cornwall. Today, the Dorrien-Smith estate still holds the lease for the island of <a href="/wiki/Tresco,_Isles_of_Scilly" title="Tresco, Isles of Scilly">Tresco</a>.\n</p>\n<ul><li>1568\xe2\x80\x931608 <a Dorrien-Smith</a> (1876\xe2\x80\x931955)</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isles_of_Scilly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Scilly_Isles_Locator_Map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Scilly_Isles_Locator_Map.png/220px-Scilly_Isles_Locator_Map.png" width="220" height="366" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Scilly_Isles_Locator_Map.png/330px-Scilly_Isles_Locator_Map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Scilly_Isles_Locator_Map.png/440px-Scilly_Isles_Locator_Map.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="1665" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Scilly_Isles_Locator_Map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Location of the Isles of Scilly (circled)</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Scilly_wards_parishes.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Scilly_wards_parishes.png/220px-Scilly_wards_parishes.png" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Scilly_wards_parishes.png/330px-Scilly_wards_parishes.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Scilly_wards_parishes.png/440px-Scilly_wards_parishes.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Scilly_wards_parishes.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The five <a href="/wiki/Wards_and_electoral_divisions_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Wards and electoral divisions of the United Kingdom">wards</a> (which are also the <a href="/wiki/Civil_parishes_in_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Civil parishes in England">civil parishes</a>) of the Isles of Scilly; red is St Agnes, blue is Bryher, orange is Tresco, green is St Martin\'s, and grey is St Mary\'s.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Isles of Scilly form an archipelago of five inhabited islands (six if <a href="/wiki/Gugh" title="Gugh">Gugh</a> is counted separately from St Agnes) and numerous other small rocky <a href="/wiki/Islet" title="Islet">islets</a> (around 140 in total) lying 45&#160;km (28&#160;mi) off <a href="/wiki/Land%27s_End" title="Land&#39;s End">Land\'s End</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-readersnatural_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-readersnatural-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The islands\' position produces a place of great contrast; the ameliorating effect of the sea, greatly influenced by the <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Current" title="North Atlantic Current">North Atlantic Current</a>, means they rarely have frost or snow, which allows local farmers to grow flowers well ahead of those in mainland Britain. The chief agricultural product is cut flowers, mostly <a href="/wiki/Daffodil" class="mw-redirect" title="Daffodil">daffodils</a>. Exposure to <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic</a> winds also means that spectacular winter gales lash the islands from time to time. This is reflected in the landscape, most clearly seen on Tresco where the lush <a href="/wiki/Tresco_Abbey_Gardens" title="Tresco Abbey Gardens">Abbey Gardens</a> on the sheltered southern end of the island contrast with the low <a href="/wiki/Calluna" title="Calluna">heather</a> and bare rock sculpted by the wind on the exposed northern end.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Natural_England" title="Natural England">Natural England</a> has designated the Isles of Scilly as <a href="/wiki/National_Character_Area" title="National Character Area">National Character Area</a> 158.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> As part of a 2002 marketing campaign, the plant conservation charity <a href="/wiki/Plantlife" title="Plantlife">Plantlife</a> chose sea thrift (<i><a href="/wiki/Armeria_maritima" title="Armeria maritima">Armeria maritima</a></i>) as the "<a href="/wiki/Floral_emblem" title="Floral emblem">county flower</a>" of the islands.<sup id="cite_ref-Thorgrim_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thorgrim-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-thrift_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thrift-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>This table provides an overview of the most important islands:\n</p>\n<table style="width:61%;" class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th style="width:23%;">Island\n</th>\n<th style="width:13%;">Population<br />(<a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Census_2001" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Census 2001">Census 2001</a>)\n</th>\n<th style="text-align:right;">&#160;\xe2\x80\x93</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">0.16</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">&#160;-</td>\n<td>&#160;\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Great_Ganilly" style="text-align:right;">&#160;-</td>\n<td>&#160;\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#ddd;">\n<td><b>Isles of Scilly</b></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">2,153</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">16.37</td>\n<td></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Hugh_Town" title="Hugh Town">Hugh Town</a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><sup>(1) </sup> Inhabited until 1855.\n</p><p>In 1975 the islands were designated as an <a href="/wiki/Area_of_Outstanding_Natural_Beauty" title="Area of Outstanding Natural Beauty">Area of Outstanding Natural Beauty</a>. The designation covers the entire archipelago, including the uninhabited islands and rocks, and is the smallest such area in the UK. The islands of Annet and Samson have large <a href="/wiki/Tern" title="Tern">terneries</a> and the islands are well populated by <a href="/wiki/Pinniped" title="Pinniped">seals</a>. The Isles of Scilly are the only British haunt of the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_white-toothed_shrew" title="Lesser white-toothed shrew">lesser white-toothed shrew</a> (<i>Crocidura suaveolens</i>), where it is known locally as a "<i>teak</i>" or "<i>teke</i>".<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The islands are famous among <a href="/wiki/Birdwatching" title="Birdwatching">birdwatchers</a> for their ability to attract rare birds from all corners of the globe. The peak time of year for this is generally in October when it is not unusual for several of the rarest birds in Europe to share this archipelago. One reason for the success of these islands in producing rarities is the extensive coverage these islands get from birdwatchers, but archipelagos are often favoured by rare birds which like to make landfall and eat there before continuing their journeys and often arrive on far-flung islands first.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tidal_influx">Tidal influx</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isles_of_Scilly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Tidal influx">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The tidal range at the Isles of Scilly is high for an open sea location; the maximum for St Mary\'s is 5.99&#160;m (19.7&#160;ft). Additionally, the inter-island waters are mostly shallow, which at <a href="/wiki/Spring_tides" class="mw-redirect" title="Spring tides">spring tides</a> allows for dry land walking between several of the islands. Many of the northern islands can be reached from Tresco, including Bryher, Samson and St Martin\'s (requires very low tides). From St Martin\'s White Island, Little Ganilly and Great Arthur are reachable. Although the sound between St Mary\'s and Tresco, The Road, is fairly shallow, it never becomes totally dry, but according to some sources it should be possible to wade at extreme low tides. Around St Mary\'s several minor islands become accessible, including Taylor\'s Island on the west coast and Tolls Island on the east coast. From Saint Agnes, Gugh becomes accessible at each low tide, via a <a href="/wiki/Tombolo" title="Tombolo">tombolo</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isles_of_Scilly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width: 19.5em; left:0;width:1.6em;height:1.5em;text-align:center"><span style="font-size:80%">51</span></div>\n<div style="color:red;position:absolute;bottom:7.88em; left:0;width:1.6em;height:1.5em;text-align:center"><span style="font-size:80%">44</span></div>\n</div></td>\n</tr>\n<tr><td colspan="12" style="padding: 2px; text-align: left; line-height: 1.5em; color: red">Average max. and min. temperatures in \xc2\xb0F</td></tr>\n<tr><td colspan="12" style="padding: 2px; text-align: left; line-height: 1.5em; color: blue">Precipitation totals in inches</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The Isles of Scilly has a <a href="/wiki/Temperate" class="mw-redirect" title="Temperate">temperate</a> <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">Oceanic climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification</a> Cfb), and has one of the mildest climates in the United Kingdom. The average annual temperature is 11.8&#160;\xc2\xb0C (53.2&#160;\xc2\xb0F) in comparison to London, where it is 11.6&#160;\xc2\xb0C (52.9&#160;\xc2\xb0F). Winters are among the warmest in the country due to the moderating effects of the ocean, and despite being on exactly the same latitude as <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg" title="Winnipeg">Winnipeg</a> in Canada, snow and frost are extremely rare. Summers are not as warm as on the mainland. The Scilly Isles are one of the sunniest areas in the southwest with on average 7 hours per day in May. The lowest temperature ever recorded was \xe2\x88\x927.2&#160;\xc2\xb0C (19.0&#160;\xc2\xb0F) and the highest was 27.8&#160;\xc2\xb0C (82.0&#160;\xc2\xb0F).<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The maximum snowfall was 23&#160;cm (9&#160;in) on 12 January 1987.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> It has never recorded a temperature below freezing between May and November.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable collapsible" style="width:90%; text-align:center; font-size:90%; line-height: 1.2em;
