<a href="/wiki/Met_Office" title="Met Office">Met Office</a><sup id="cite_ref-YYTstats_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YYTstats-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isles_of_Scilly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Victoria_history_of_the_county_of_Cornwall_(1906)_(14754540266).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/The_Victoria_history_of_the_county_of_Cornwall_%281906%29_%2814754540266%29.jpg/220px-The_Victoria_history_of_the_county_of_Cornwall_%281906%29_%2814754540266%29.jpg" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/The_Victoria_history_of_the_county_of_Cornwall_%281906%29_%2814754540266%29.jpg/330px-The_Victoria_history_of_the_county_of_Cornwall_%281906%29_%2814754540266%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/The_Victoria_history_of_the_county_of_Cornwall_%281906%29_%2814754540266%29.jpg/440px-The_Victoria_history_of_the_county_of_Cornwall_%281906%29_%2814754540266%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4216" data-file-height="3022" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Victoria_history_of_the_county_of_Cornwall_(1906)_(14754540266).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Geological map of western Cornwall, with the Isles of Scilly (inset)</div></div></div>\n<p>All the islands of Scilly are all composed of <a href="/wiki/Granite" title="Granite">granite</a> rock of early <a href="/wiki/Permian" title="Permian">Permian</a> age, an exposed part of the <a href="/wiki/Cornubian_batholith" title="Cornubian batholith">Cornubian batholith</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Irish_Sea_Glacier" title="Irish Sea Glacier">Irish Sea Glacier</a> terminated just to the north of the Isles of Scilly during the last <a href="/wiki/Ice_Age" class="mw-redirect" title="Ice Age">Ice Age</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hiemstra,_et_al._2006_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hiemstra,_et_al._2006-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Scourse_1991_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scourse_1991-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fauna">Fauna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isles_of_Scilly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Fauna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Fauna_of_the_Isles_of_Scilly" title="Fauna of the Isles of Scilly">Fauna of the Isles of Scilly</a></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isles_of_Scilly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ScillonianCross.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/ScillonianCross.svg/220px-ScillonianCross.svg.png" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/ScillonianCross.svg/330px-ScillonianCross.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/ScillonianCross.svg/440px-ScillonianCross.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ScillonianCross.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Scillonian Cross, the flag of the Isles of Scilly.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Cornwall.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Flag_of_Cornwall.svg/220px-Flag_of_Cornwall.svg.png" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Flag_of_Cornwall.svg/330px-Flag_of_Cornwall.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Flag_of_Cornwall.svg/440px-Flag_of_Cornwall.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="400" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Cornwall.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Saint_Piran%27s_Flag" title="Saint Piran&#39;s Flag">Saint Piran\'s Cross</a>, the flag of Cornwall. The Isles of Scilly were one of the <a href="/wiki/Hundreds_of_Cornwall" title="Hundreds of Cornwall">Hundreds of Cornwall</a>, and although they have been administratively separate since 1890, they are still part of the ceremonial county of <a href="/wiki/Cornwall" title="Cornwall">Cornwall</a>.</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_government">National government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isles_of_Scilly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: National government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Politically, the islands are part of England, one of the four <a href="/wiki/Countries_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Countries of the United Kingdom">countries of the United Kingdom</a>. They are represented in the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">UK Parliament</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/St_Ives_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="St Ives (UK Parliament constituency)">St Ives constituency</a>. As part of the United Kingdom, the islands are part of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and are represented in the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> as part of the multi-member <a href="/wiki/South_West_England_(European_Parliament_constituency)" title="South West England (European Parliament constituency)">South West England constituency</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_government">Local government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isles_of_Scilly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Local government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_Isles_of_Scilly" title="Council of the Isles of Scilly">Council of the Isles of Scilly</a></div>\n<p>Historically, the Isles of Scilly were administered as one of the <a href="/wiki/Hundreds_of_Cornwall" title="Hundreds of Cornwall">hundreds of Cornwall</a>, although the Cornwall <a href="/wiki/Quarter_sessions" class="mw-redirect" title="Quarter sessions">quarter sessions</a> had limited jurisdiction there. For judicial purposes, <a href="/wiki/High_Sheriff" class="mw-redirect" title="High Sheriff">shrievalty</a> purposes, and <a href="/wiki/Lord_Lieutenant" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Lieutenant">lieutenancy</a> purposes, the Isles of Scilly are "deemed to form part of the county of Cornwall".<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The archipelago is part of the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Cornwall" title="Duchy of Cornwall">Duchy of Cornwall</a><sup id="cite_ref-duchysite_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-duchysite-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> \xe2\x80\x93 the duchy owns the freehold of most of the land on the islands and the duke exercises certain formal rights and privileges across the territory, as he does in Cornwall proper.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_Act_1888" title="Local Government Act 1888">Local Government Act 1888</a> allowed the <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_Board" title="Local Government Board">Local Government Board</a> to establish in the Isles of Scilly "councils and other local authorities separate from those of the county of Cornwall"... "for the application to the islands of any act touching local government." Accordingly, in 1890 the <i>Isles of Scilly Rural District Council</i> (the RDC) was formed as a <i><a href="/wiki/Sui_generis" title="Sui generis">sui generis</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Unitary_Authority" class="mw-redirect" title="Unitary Authority">unitary authority</a>, outside the <a href="/wiki/Administrative_county" title="Administrative county">administrative county</a> of Cornwall. Cornwall County Council provided some services to the Isles, for which the RDC made financial contributions. The Isles of Scilly Order 1930<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> granted the Council the "powers, duties and liabilities" of a <a href="/wiki/County_council" title="County council">county council</a>. Section 265 of the <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_Act_1972" title="Local Government Act 1972">Local Government Act 1972</a> allowed for the continued existence of the RDC, but renamed as the <i>Council of the Isles of Scilly</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-iosuatt_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iosuatt-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-iosrdtt_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iosrdtt-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>This unusual status also means that much administrative law (for example relating to the functions of local authorities, the health service and other public bodies) that applies in the rest of England applies in modified form in the islands.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Council of the Isles of Scilly is a separate authority to the <a href="/wiki/Cornwall_Council" title="Cornwall Council">Cornwall Council</a> unitary authority, and as such the islands are not part of the administrative county of Cornwall. However the islands are still considered to be part of the <a href="/wiki/Ceremonial_counties_of_England" title="Ceremonial counties of England">ceremonial county</a> of Cornwall.\n</p><p>With a total population of just over 2,000, the council represents fewer inhabitants than many English <a href="/wiki/Parish_councils_in_England" title="Parish councils in England">parish councils</a>, and is by far the smallest English unitary council. As of  2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Isles_of_Scilly&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, 130 people are employed <a href="/wiki/Full-time_equivalent" title="Full-time equivalent">full-time</a> by the council<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> to provide local services (including water supply and <a href="/wiki/Air_traffic_control" title="Air traffic control">air traffic control</a>). These numbers are significant, in that almost 10% of the adult population of the islands is directly linked to the council, as an employee or a councillor.<sup id="cite_ref-acca2002_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-acca2002-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Council consists of 21 elected councillors \xe2\x80\x94 13 of whom are returned by the <a href="/wiki/Wards_and_electoral_divisions_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Wards and electoral divisions of the United Kingdom">ward</a> of St Mary\'s, and two from each of four "off-island" wards (St Martin\'s, St Agnes, Bryher, and Tresco). The <a href="/wiki/Isles_of_Scilly_Council_election,_2013" class="mw-redirect" title="Isles of Scilly Council election, 2013">latest elections</a> took place on 2 May 2013; all 20 elected were <a href="/wiki/Independent_(politician)" class="mw-redirect" title="Independent (politician)">independents</a> (one seat remained vacant).<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The council is headquartered at Town Hall, by The Parade park in <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Town" title="Hugh Town">Hugh Town</a>, and also performs the administrative functions of the <a href="/wiki/Area_of_Outstanding_Natural_Beauty" title="Area of Outstanding Natural Beauty">AONB</a> Partnership<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Inshore_Fisheries_and_Conservation_Authority" title="Inshore Fisheries and Conservation Authority">Inshore Fisheries and Conservation Authority</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Some aspects of local government are shared with Cornwall, including <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_Cornwall" title="Healthcare in Cornwall">health</a>, and the Council of the Isles of Scilly together with <a href="/wiki/Cornwall_Council" title="Cornwall Council">Cornwall Council</a> form a <a href="/wiki/Local_Enterprise_Partnership" class="mw-redirect" title="Local Enterprise Partnership">Local Enterprise Partnership</a>. In July 2015 a <a href="/wiki/Devolution_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Devolution in the United Kingdom">devolution</a> deal was announced by the <a href="/wiki/Second_Cameron_ministry" title="Second Cameron ministry">government</a> under which Cornwall Council and the Council of the Isles of Scilly are to create a plan to bring health and social care services together under local control. The Local Enterprise Partnership is also to be bolstered.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flags">Flags</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isles_of_Scilly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Flags">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Mary%27s_Church,_Hugh_Town.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/St_Mary%27s_Church%2C_Hugh_Town.JPG/220px-St_Mary%27s_Church%2C_Hugh_Town.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/St_Mary%27s_Church%2C_Hugh_Town.JPG/330px-St_Mary%27s_Church%2C_Hugh_Town.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/St_Mary%27s_Church%2C_Hugh_Town.JPG/440px-St_Mary%27s_Church%2C_Hugh_Town.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Mary%27s_Church,_Hugh_Town.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Scillonian Cross flying above <a href="/wiki/St_Mary%27s_Church,_St_Mary%27s" title="St Mary&#39;s Church, St Mary&#39;s">St Mary\'s Church</a> in Hugh Town.</div></div></div>\n<p>Two flags are used to represent Scilly:\n</p>\n<ul><li>The Scillonian Cross, selected by readers of <i>Scilly News</i> in a 2002 vote and then registered with the <a href="/wiki/Flag_Institute" title="Flag Institute">Flag Institute</a> as the flag of the islands.<sup id="cite_ref-bofflag_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bofflag-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sccross_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sccross-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-flaginstitute_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flaginstitute-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>The flag of the Council of the Isles of Scilly, which incorporates the council\'s logo and represents the council.<sup id="cite_ref-bofflag_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bofflag-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>An adapted version of the old Board of Ordnance flag has also been used, after it was left behind when munitions were removed from the isles. The "Cornish Ensign" (the Cornish cross with the Union Jack in the canton) has also been used.<sup id="cite_ref-bofflag_41-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bofflag-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cornens_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cornens-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Emergency_services">Emergency services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isles_of_Scilly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Emergency services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Isles of Scilly form part of the <a href="/wiki/Devon_and_Cornwall_Police" title="Devon and Cornwall Police">Devon and Cornwall Police</a> force area. There is a police station in <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Town" title="Hugh Town">Hugh Town</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Cornwall_Air_Ambulance" title="Cornwall Air Ambulance">Cornwall Air Ambulance</a> helicopter provides cover to the islands.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The islands have their own independent fire brigade \xe2\x80\x93 the <a href="/wiki/Isles_of_Scilly_Fire_and_Rescue_Service" title="Isles of Scilly Fire and Rescue Service">Isles of Scilly Fire and Rescue Service</a> \xe2\x80\x93 which is staffed entirely by retained firefighters on all the inhabited islands.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isles_of_Scilly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_on_the_Isles_of_Scilly" title="List of schools on the Isles of Scilly">List of schools on the Isles of Scilly</a></div>\n<p>Education is available on the islands up to age 16. There is one school, the <a href="/wiki/Five_Islands_School" title="Five Islands School">Five Islands School</a>, which provides primary schooling at sites on St Agnes, St Mary\'s, St Martin\'s and Tresco, and secondary schooling at a site on St Mary\'s. Secondary students from outside St Mary\'s live at a school boarding house (Mundesley House) during the week. In 2004, 92.9% of pupils (26 out of 28) achieved five or more <a href="/wiki/GCSE" class="mw-redirect" title="GCSE">GCSEs</a> at grade C and above, compared to the English average of 53.7%.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Sixteen- to eighteen-year-olds are entitled to a free <a href="/wiki/Sixth_form" title="Sixth form">sixth form</a> place at a state school or sixth form college on the mainland, and are provided with free flights and a grant towards accommodation. Suitably qualified students after age eighteen attend universities and colleges on the mainland.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isles_of_Scilly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_context">Historical context</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isles_of_Scilly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Historical context">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Since the mid-18th century the Scillonian economy has relied on trade with the mainland and beyond as a means of sustaining its population. Over the years the nature of this trade has varied, due to wider economic and political factors that have seen the rise and fall of industries such as <a href="/wiki/Kelp" title="Kelp">kelp</a> harvesting, <a href="/wiki/Harbour_pilot" class="mw-redirect" title="Harbour pilot">pilotage</a>, smuggling, fishing, <a href="/wiki/Shipbuilding" title="Shipbuilding">shipbuilding</a> and, latterly, <a href="/wiki/Floriculture" title="Floriculture">flower farming</a>. In a 1987 study of the Scillonian economy, Neate found that many farms on the islands were struggling to remain profitable due to increasing costs and strong competition from overseas producers, with resulting diversification into tourism. Recent statistics suggest that agriculture on the islands now represents less than 2% of all employment.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-partnership_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-partnership-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isles_of_Scilly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Martins_Daymark.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/St_Martins_Daymark.jpg/220px-St_Martins_Daymark.jpg" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/St_Martins_Daymark.jpg/330px-St_Martins_Daymark.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/St_Martins_Daymark.jpg/440px-St_Martins_Daymark.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2133" data-file-height="1565" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Martins_Daymark.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Daymark" title="Daymark">Daymark</a> (daylight version of a <a href="/wiki/Lighthouse" title="Lighthouse">lighthouse</a>) on St Martins, the nearest point to the mainland of <a href="/wiki/Cornwall" title="Cornwall">Cornwall</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Today, tourism is estimated to account for 85% of the islands\' income. The islands have been successful in attracting this investment due to their special environment, favourable summer climate, relaxed culture, efficient co-ordination of tourism providers and good transport links by sea and air to the mainland, uncommon in scale to similar-sized island communities.<sup id="cite_ref-council_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-council-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-touristboard_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-touristboard-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The majority of visitors stay on <a href="/wiki/St_Mary%27s,_Isles_of_Scilly" title="St Mary&#39;s, Isles of Scilly">St Mary\'s</a>, which has a concentration of holiday accommodation and other amenities. Of the other inhabited islands, <a href="/wiki/Tresco,_Isles_of_Scilly" title="Tresco, Isles of Scilly">Tresco</a> is run as a timeshare resort, and is consequently the most obviously tourist-oriented. <a href="/wiki/Bryher,_Isles_of_Scilly" class="mw-redirect" title="Bryher, Isles of Scilly">Bryher</a> and <a href="/wiki/St_Martin%27s,_Isles_of_Scilly" title="St Martin&#39;s, Isles of Scilly">St Martin\'s</a> are more unspoilt, although each has a hotel and other accommodation. <a href="/wiki/St_Agnes,_Isles_of_Scilly" title="St Agnes, Isles of Scilly">St Agnes</a> has no hotel and is the least-developed of the inhabited islands.\n</p><p>The islands\' economy is highly dependent on tourism, even by the standards of other island communities. \xe2\x80\x9cThe concentration [on] a small number of sectors is typical of most similarly sized UK island communities. However, it is the degree of concentration, which is distinctive along with the overall importance of tourism within the economy as a whole and the very limited manufacturing base that stands out.\xe2\x80\x9d<sup id="cite_ref-partnership_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-partnership-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Tourism is also a highly seasonal industry owing to its reliance on outdoor recreation, and the lower number of tourists in winter results in a significant constriction of the islands\' commercial activities. However, the tourist season benefits from an extended period of business in October when many <a href="/wiki/Birding" class="mw-redirect" title="Birding">birdwatchers</a> ("birders") arrive.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ornithology">Ornithology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isles_of_Scilly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Ornithology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Because of its position, Scilly is the first landing for many migrant birds, including extreme rarities from North America and <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a>. Scilly is situated far into the Atlantic Ocean, so many American vagrant birds will make first European landfall in the archipelago.\n</p><p>Scilly is responsible for many firsts for Britain, and is particularly good at producing vagrant American <a href="/wiki/Passerine" title="Passerine">passerines</a>. If an extremely rare bird turns up, the island will see a significant increase in numbers of birders. This type of birding, chasing after rare birds, is called "<a href="/wiki/Birdwatching#Birding,_birdwatching_and_twitching" title="Birdwatching">twitching</a>".\n</p><p>The islands are home to <a href="/wiki/Ornithologist" class="mw-redirect" title="Ornithologist">ornithologist</a> <a href="/wiki/Will_Wagstaff" title="Will Wagstaff">Will Wagstaff</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Employment">Employment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isles_of_Scilly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Employment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The predominance of tourism means that "tourism is by far the main sector throughout each of the individual islands, in terms of employment... [and] this is much greater than other remote and rural areas in the United Kingdom\xe2\x80\x9d. Tourism accounts for approximately 63% of all employment.<sup id="cite_ref-partnership_48-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-partnership-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Businesses dependent on tourism, with the exception of a few hotels, tend to be small enterprises typically employing fewer than four people; many of these are family run, suggesting an entrepreneurial culture among the local population.<sup id="cite_ref-partnership_48-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-partnership-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> However, much of the work generated by this, with the exception of management, is low skilled and thus poorly paid, especially for those involved in cleaning, catering and retail.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Because of the seasonality of tourism, many jobs on the islands are seasonal and part-time, so work cannot be guaranteed throughout the year. Some islanders take up other temporary jobs \xe2\x80\x98out of season\xe2\x80\x99 to compensate for this. Due to a lack of local casual labour at peak holiday times, many of the larger employers accommodate guest workers, who come to the islands for the summer to have a \xe2\x80\x98<a href="/wiki/Volunteer_travel" class="mw-redirect" title="Volunteer travel">working holiday</a>\xe2\x80\x99.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taxation">Taxation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isles_of_Scilly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Taxation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The islands were not subject to <a href="/wiki/Income_Tax" class="mw-redirect" title="Income Tax">income tax</a> until 1954, and there was no motor <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_excise_duty" class="mw-redirect" title="Vehicle excise duty">vehicle excise duty</a> levied until 1971.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isles_of_Scilly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Electric_golf_buggy_on_St_Marys.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Electric_golf_buggy_on_St_Marys.jpg/220px-Electric_golf_buggy_on_St_Marys.jpg" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Electric_golf_buggy_on_St_Marys.jpg/330px-Electric_golf_buggy_on_St_Marys.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Electric_golf_buggy_on_St_Marys.jpg/440px-Electric_golf_buggy_on_St_Marys.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1936" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Electric_golf_buggy_on_St_Marys.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An electric golf buggy on St Mary\'s; these are road licensed and available for hire, as are bicycles, for use on public roads on the island.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RMV_Scillonian_III_docked_at_St_Mary%27s_harbour.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/RMV_Scillonian_III_docked_at_St_Mary%27s_harbour.jpg/220px-RMV_Scillonian_III_docked_at_St_Mary%27s_harbour.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/RMV_Scillonian_III_docked_at_St_Mary%27s_harbour.jpg/330px-RMV_Scillonian_III_docked_at_St_Mary%27s_harbour.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/RMV_Scillonian_III_docked_at_St_Mary%27s_harbour.jpg/440px-RMV_Scillonian_III_docked_at_St_Mary%27s_harbour.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1808" data-file-height="1202" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RMV_Scillonian_III_docked_at_St_Mary%27s_harbour.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Scillonian_III" class="mw-redirect" title="Scillonian III">Scillonian III</a></i> in St Mary\'s Harbour</div></div></div>\n<p>St Mary\'s is the only island with a significant road network and the only island with public highways; in 2005 there were 619 registered vehicles on the island. The island also has <a href="/wiki/Taxicab" title="Taxicab">taxis</a> and a tour <a href="/wiki/Bus" title="Bus">bus</a>. Vehicles on the islands are exempt from annual <a href="/wiki/MOT_test" title="MOT test">MOT tests</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Roads and streets across Scilly have very few signs or markings, and route numbers (of the three <a href="/wiki/A_roads_in_Great_Britain" class="mw-redirect" title="A roads in Great Britain">A roads</a> on St Mary\'s) are not marked at all.\n</p><p>Air access to the islands is via <a href="/wiki/St_Mary%27s_Airport_(Isles_of_Scilly)" class="mw-redirect" title="St Mary&#39;s Airport (Isles of Scilly)">St Mary\'s Airport</a>. <a href="/wiki/Fixed-wing_aircraft" title="Fixed-wing aircraft">Fixed-wing aircraft</a> services, operated by <a href="/wiki/Isles_of_Scilly_Skybus" title="Isles of Scilly Skybus">Isles of Scilly Skybus</a>, operate from <a href="/wiki/Land%27s_End_Airport" title="Land&#39;s End Airport">Land\'s End</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newquay_Cornwall_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Newquay Cornwall Airport">Newquay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Exeter_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Exeter International Airport">Exeter</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-iossb_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iossb-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>The scheduled <a href="/wiki/Helicopter" title="Helicopter">helicopter</a> service, which previously linked <a href="/wiki/Penzance_Heliport" title="Penzance Heliport">Penzance Heliport</a> with St Mary\'s Airport and <a href="/wiki/Tresco_Heliport" title="Tresco Heliport">Tresco Heliport</a>, ceased at the end of October 2012. A new heliport is currently under construction in Penzance and helicopter services to Tresco and St Mary\'s are expected to commence in 2019 or 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By sea, the <a href="/wiki/Isles_of_Scilly_Steamship_Company" title="Isles of Scilly Steamship Company">Isles of Scilly Steamship Company</a> provides a passenger and cargo service from <a href="/wiki/Penzance" title="Penzance">Penzance</a> to St Mary\'s, which is currently operated by the <i><a href="/wiki/Scillonian_III" class="mw-redirect" title="Scillonian III">Scillonian III</a></i> passenger ferry, supported until summer 2017 by the <i><a href="/wiki/Gry_Maritha" title="Gry Maritha">Gry Maritha</a></i> cargo vessel and now by the <i>Mali Rose</i>. The other islands are linked to St. Mary\'s by a network of inter-island <a href="/wiki/Launch_(boat)" title="Launch (boat)">launches</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ioss_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ioss-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/St_Mary%27s_Harbour" class="mw-redirect" title="St Mary&#39;s Harbour">St Mary\'s Harbour</a> is the principal harbour of the Isles of Scilly, and is located in Hugh Town.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tenure">Tenure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isles_of_Scilly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Tenure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Freehold_(law)" title="Freehold (law)">freehold land</a> of the islands is the property of the Duchy of Cornwall (except for <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Town" title="Hugh Town">Hugh Town</a> on St Mary\'s, which was sold to the inhabitants in 1949). The duchy also holds 3,921 acres (16&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) as duchy property, part of the duchy\'s landholding.<sup id="cite_ref-landholding_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-landholding-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> All the uninhabited islands, islets and rocks and much of the untenanted land on the inhabited islands is managed by the <a href="/wiki/Isles_of_Scilly_Wildlife_Trust" title="Isles of Scilly Wildlife Trust">Isles of Scilly Wildlife Trust</a>, which leases these lands from the Duchy for the rent of one daffodil per year.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> The trust currently has four full-time salaried staff and 12 trustees, who are all residents of the Isles. The full trust board is responsible for policy whilst a management team is responsible for day-to-day administration. Its small income and the small number of staff have led to the trust adopting a policy of recruiting volunteers to help it carry out its extensive work programme. While volunteers of all ages are welcome, most are young people who are studying for qualifications in related fields, such as conservation and land management.\n</p><p>Limited housing availability is a contentious yet critical issue for the Isles of Scilly, especially as it affects the feasibility of residency on the islands. Few properties are privately owned, with many units being let by the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Cornwall" title="Duchy of Cornwall">Duchy of Cornwall</a>, the council and a few by <a href="/wiki/Housing_association" title="Housing association">housing associations</a>. The management of these subsequently affects the possibility of residency on the islands.<sup id="cite_ref-martin_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-martin-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Duchy_Tenants_Association" title="Duchy Tenants Association">Duchy Tenants Association</a> was formed in 1996 by a number of tenants of the Duchy of Cornwall.\n</p><p>Housing demand outstrips supply, a problem compounded by restrictions on further development designed to protect the islands\' unique environment and prevent the infrastructural carrying capacity from being exceeded. This has pushed up the prices of the few private properties that become available and, significantly for the majority of the islands\' populations, it has also affected the rental sector where rates have likewise drastically increased.<sup id="cite_ref-SWHB_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SWHB-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fleming_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fleming-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>High housing costs pose significant problems for the local population, especially as local incomes (in Cornwall) are only 70% of the national average, whilst house prices are almost \xc2\xa35,000 higher than the national average. This in turn affects the retention of \xe2\x80\x98key workers\xe2\x80\x99 and the younger generation, which consequently affects the viability of schools and other essential community services.<sup id="cite_ref-council_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-council-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fleming_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fleming-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The limited access to housing provokes strong local politics. It is often assumed that tourism is to blame for this, attracting newcomers to the area who can afford to outbid locals for available housing. Many buildings are used for tourist accommodation which reduces the number available for local residents. Second homes are also thought to account for a significant proportion of the housing stock, leaving many buildings empty for much of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Cornishman_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Cornishman-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isles_of_Scilly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="People">People</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isles_of_Scilly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: People">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Cornish_people" title="Cornish people">Cornish people</a> and <a href="/wiki/English_people" title="English people">English people</a></div>\n<p>According to the 2001 UK census, 97% of the population of the islands are <a href="/wiki/White_British" title="White British">white British</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-ONS1_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ONS1-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> with nearly 93% of the inhabitants born in the islands, in mainland Cornwall or elsewhere in England.<sup id="cite_ref-ONS2_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ONS2-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Since EU enlargement in 2004, a number of <a href="/wiki/A8_countries" title="A8 countries">eastern Europeans</a> have moved to the island, joining the Australians, New Zealanders and South Africans who traditionally made up most of the islands\' overseas workers. By 2005, their numbers were estimated at nearly 100 out of a total population of just over 2,000.<sup id="cite_ref-Guard_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guard-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> The Isles have also been referred to as "the land that crime forgot", reflecting lower crime levels than national averages.<sup id="cite_ref-Mawby_2002_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mawby_2002-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isles_of_Scilly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>One continuing legacy of the isles\' past is <a href="/wiki/Cornish_pilot_gig" title="Cornish pilot gig">gig racing</a>, wherein fast rowing boats ("gigs") with crews of six (or in one case, seven) race between the main islands. Gig racing has been said to derive from the race to collect <a href="/wiki/Marine_salvage" title="Marine salvage">salvage</a> from shipwrecks on the rocks around Scilly, but the race was actually to deliver a <a href="/wiki/Harbour_pilot" class="mw-redirect" title="Harbour pilot">pilot</a> onto incoming vessels, to guide them through the hazardous reefs and shallows. (The boats are correctly termed "pilot gigs"). The <a href="/wiki/World_Pilot_Gig_Championships" title="World Pilot Gig Championships">World Pilot Gig Championships</a> are held annually over the May Day bank holiday weekend. The event originally involved crews from the Islands and a few crews from Cornwall, but in the intervening years the number of gigs attending has increased, with crews coming from all over the South-West and further afield.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Isles of Scilly feature what is reportedly the smallest <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> league in the world, the <a href="/wiki/Isles_of_Scilly_Football_League" title="Isles of Scilly Football League">Isles of Scilly Football League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> The league\'s two clubs, Woolpack Wanderers and Garrison Gunners, play each other 17 times each season and compete for two cups and for the league title. The league was a launching pad for the <a href="/wiki/Adidas" title="Adidas">Adidas</a> "Dream Big" Campaign<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> in which a number of famous professional footballers (including <a href="/wiki/David_Beckham" title="David Beckham">David Beckham</a>) arrive on the island to coach the local children\'s side. The two share a ground, Garrison Field, but travel to the mainland for part of the year to play other non-professional clubs.\n</p><p>In December 2006, <a href="/wiki/Sport_England" title="Sport England">Sport England</a> published a survey which revealed that residents of the Isles of Scilly were the most active in England in sports and other fitness activities. 32% of the population participate at least three times a week for 30 minutes or more.<sup id="cite_ref-mostact_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mostact-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There is a <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">golf</a> club with a nine-hole course (each with two tees) situated on the island of St Mary\'s, near <a href="/wiki/Porthloo" title="Porthloo">Porthloo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Telegraph,_Isles_of_Scilly" title="Telegraph, Isles of Scilly">Telegraph</a>. The club was founded in 1904 and is open to visitors.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isles_of_Scilly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The islands are served by a radio and television transmitter at Telegraph, on St Mary\'s, which is a relay of the main transmitter at Redruth (Cornwall) and broadcasts <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio" title="BBC Radio">BBC Radio</a> <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_1" title="BBC Radio 1">1</a>, <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_2" title="BBC Radio 2">2</a>, <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_3" title="BBC Radio 3">3</a>, <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_4" title="BBC Radio 4">4</a> and <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_Cornwall" title="BBC Radio Cornwall">BBC Radio Cornwall</a> and the range of <a href="/wiki/Freeview_(UK)" title="Freeview (UK)">Freeview</a> television and BBC radio channels known as \'Freeview Light\'.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Radio_Scilly" title="Radio Scilly">Radio Scilly</a>, a community radio station, was launched in September 2007.\n</p><p>There is no local newspaper; <i><a href="/wiki/Scilly_Now_%26_Then" title="Scilly Now &amp; Then">Scilly Now &amp; Then</a></i> is a free community magazine produced eight times a year and is available to mainland subscribers while <i>The Scillonian</i> is published twice yearly and reports matters of local interest. There is an active news forum on the news and information websites scillytoday.com<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> and thisisscilly.com.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Internet access is available across the inhabited islands by means of superfast fibre broadband by BT. The islands connected via fibre are St. Mary\'s, Tresco and Bryher. St. Martins, St. Agnes and Gugh are connected via a new fibre microwave link from St. Mary\'s, with fibre cabinets on each island, including Gugh.\n</p><p>Mobile phone coverage is available across the archipelago, with 2G, 3G and 4G services available across all islands, although coverage does vary between operators. Vodafone and O2 provide strong 4G coverage across all the islands, whilst EE\'s is somewhat limited beyond Gugh towards St. Agnes. Three provide 3G coverage to all the islands, and 4G is due shortly.\n</p><p>The Isles of Scilly were featured on the TV programme <i><a href="/wiki/Seven_Natural_Wonders" title="Seven Natural Wonders">Seven Natural Wonders</a></i> as one of the wonders of South West England. Since 2007 the islands have featured in the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> series <i><a href="/wiki/An_Island_Parish" title="An Island Parish">An Island Parish</a></i>, following various real-life stories and featuring in particular the newly appointed <i>Chaplain to the Isles of Scilly</i>. A 12-part series was filmed in 2007 and first broadcast on <i><a href="/wiki/BBC2" class="mw-redirect" title="BBC2">BBC2</a></i> in January 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-iparish_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iparish-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> After Reverend David Easton left the islands in 2009, the series continued under the same name but focused elsewhere.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Novels">Novels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isles_of_Scilly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Novels">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The heroine of <a href="/wiki/Walter_Besant" title="Walter Besant">Walter Besant</a>\'s novel <i>Armorel of Lyonesse</i> came from Samson, and about half the action of the novel takes place in the Isles of Scilly.\n</p><p>The events of <a href="/wiki/Nevil_Shute" title="Nevil Shute">Nevil Shute</a>\'s novel <i><a href="/wiki/Marazan" title="Marazan">Marazan</a></i> occur, in part, around these islands.\n</p><p>Five children\'s books written by <a href="/wiki/Michael_Morpurgo" title="Michael Morpurgo">Michael Morpurgo</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Why_the_Whales_Came" title="Why the Whales Came">Why the Whales Came</a></i>, <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Sleeping_Sword&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="The Sleeping Sword (page does not exist)">The Sleeping Sword</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wreck_of_the_Zanzibar" title="The Wreck of the Zanzibar">The Wreck of the Zanzibar</a></i>, <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arthur,_High_King_of_Britain&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Arthur, High King of Britain (page does not exist)">Arthur, High King of Britain</a></i> and <i>Listen to the Moon</i> are set around the Isles of Scilly.\n</p><p><i>The Riddle of Samson</i>, a novel by Andrew Garve (a pen name of <a href="/wiki/Paul_Winterton" title="Paul Winterton">Paul Winterton</a>) is set mainly around the Isles of Scilly.\n</p><p>In <i>Jacob\'s Room</i>, by Virginia Woolf, the hero and a friend of his sail around the islands.\n</p><p>The novels that make up <i>The Cortes Trilogy</i> by John Paul Davis take place in the Isles of Scilly.\n</p><p><i>Stone In the Blood</i><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> by Colin Jordan and David England is set on the islands both in 1974 and the Iron Age, when most of Scilly was still one joined landmass.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Song">Song</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isles_of_Scilly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Song">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Scilly is mentioned in the traditional British naval song "<a href="/wiki/Spanish_Ladies" title="Spanish Ladies">Spanish Ladies</a>".\n</p><p>Scilly is mentioned in the song "Phenomenal Cat" by The Kinks on their album <a href="/wiki/The_Kinks_are_the_Village_Green_Preservation_Society" class="mw-redirect" title="The Kinks are the Village Green Preservation Society">The Kinks are the Village Green Preservation Society</a>.\n</p><p>Isles of Scilly is a song by the Icelandic artist Catmanic.  <sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isles_of_Scilly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Augustus_John_Smith_(1804-1872).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Augustus_John_Smith_%281804-1872%29.jpg/220px-Augustus_John_Smith_%281804-1872%29.jpg" width="220" height="314" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3e/Augustus_John_Smith_%281804-1872%29.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="329" data-file-height="469" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Augustus_John_Smith_(1804-1872).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Augustus John Smith 1804-1872</div></div></div>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Saint_Lide" title="Saint Lide">Saint Lide</a> was a bishop <sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> who lived on the island of St Helen\'s in the Isles of Scilly.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/John_Godolphin" title="John Godolphin">John Godolphin</a> (1617 in Scilly \xe2\x80\x93 1678) <sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> was an English jurist and writer, an admiralty judge under the Commonwealth.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Augustus_Smith_(politician)" title="Augustus Smith (politician)">Augustus John Smith</a> (1804 in London \xe2\x80\x93 1872 in Plymouth) <sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> was Lord Proprietor of the Isles of Scilly for over thirty years. In 1834 he acquired the lease on the Isles of Scilly from the Duchy of Cornwall for \xc2\xa320,000. He was Liberal MP for Truro from 1857 to 1865.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sir_Frederick_Hervey-Bathurst,_3rd_Baronet" title="Sir Frederick Hervey-Bathurst, 3rd Baronet">Sir Frederick Hervey-Bathurst, 3rd Baronet</a> (1807 in Scilly \xe2\x80\x93 1881 in Wiltshire) was a famous English cricketer <sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/John_Edmund_Sharrock_Moore" title="John Edmund Sharrock Moore">John Edmund Sharrock Moore</a> ARCS (1870 in Rossendale \xe2\x80\x93 1947 in Penzance) was an English biologist, best known for leading two expeditions to Tanganyika. During the 1920s he moved to Tresco.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/David_Hunt_(ornithologist)" title="David Hunt (ornithologist)">David Hunt</a> (1934 in Devonport \xe2\x80\x93 1985 in India) was an English ornithologist and horticulturalist in Tresco and at the Island Hotel where he became the gardener in 1964. He was killed by a tiger in India</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Stella_Turk" title="Stella Turk">Stella Turk</a>, MBE (1925 Scilly \xe2\x80\x93 2017 in Camborne) was a British zoologist, naturalist, and conservationist. She was known for her activities in marine biology and conservation, particularly as it applies to marine molluscs and mammals.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sam_Llewellyn" title="Sam Llewellyn">Sam Llewellyn</a> (born 1948 in Tresco) <sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> is a British author of literature for children and adults.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Stephen_Richard_Menheniott" class="mw-redirect" title="Stephen Richard Menheniott">Stephen Richard Menheniott</a> (1957 \xe2\x80\x93 1976) was an 18-year-old English man with learning difficulties who was murdered by his father on the Isles of Scilly in 1976</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Malcolm_Bell" title="Malcolm Bell">Malcolm Bell</a> (born 1969 in Hugh Town) is a former English cricketer. Bell was a right-handed batsman who bowled right-arm medium pace.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span
